< Text>
As a San Diego designer for 21 years RUG EXPO is my first choice in referring my clients for an area rug.  They have an excellent choice with great pricing on a large selection of handmade, machine and custom rugs.   They have plenty of help to flip the rugs for easy viewing.  Laying the rug out on the floor is essential prior to purchasing a rug.  The light on the grain will give you the most accurate results before purchasing the rug.  They are always so accommodating to all of my clients as they always want to ensure your satisfaction.
Lilly and her husband are owners and take great pride in their business.  They are a team which delivers excellent customer service, knowledgeable in their profession and very accommodating....All the reasons I will continue to refer my clients to RUG EXPO.
Terri Wise, Interior Makeovers< /Text>

Where to begin...
This is the best rug place I have ever been to. I know, I know--that seems ridiculous. Have you been to every rug store?? Well when you're redoing your floors and need area rugs galore, you shop around A LOT.

The selection is amazing and they have a range of price points (we left with six rugs and will be back for more). But what's really wonderful besides the selection are the employees. Ben, more specifically. He was very kind and not pushy at all. He showed us a good selection, able to pinpoint both my husband and mines very eclectic taste.

What I love is that Ben really took the time to engage with us and went above and beyond with making sure we were absolutely satisfied with our purchases. It was a wonderful experience and who knew that rug shopping would be fun.

As I wrote, my husband and I will be back shortly to pick out more rugs from Ben. If you're looking for a good price and great quality, this is the place to go!

Thank you Ben!!</review>

< Text>
This place was about 90% full and they still made us wait 5 minutes for a table.  The busboy was very friendly but we didn't see our waitress much.  The food was good, but not enough to make my kids feel like they HAD to come back any time soon.  It then took a while to get our check and to get my credit card back.  If you like the old fashioned breakfast, it's a great place to eat.  I got the eggs Benedict with avocado and was really impressed with the ham... especially because I don't really like ham.  The busboy told us that the pancakes are really popular, which my kids ordered, but they didn't feel the pancakes were any different than most pancakes.  It's a bit out of the way but it's decent for breakfast fare.</Text>

<userid>105692744256480109238<//userid>< username>
Chelsea Madren<//username>
<date>1461889682915< /date>< rating>
5</rating>
< review>
Chilaquiles and Eggs ($8.50) is crispy tortilla strips tossed with onion and tomato, topped with red salsa and cheese, served with sour cream and your choice of either home fries, hash browns, refried beans, sliced tomatoes, cottage cheese, or fresh fruit. It also comes with your choice of toast, English muffin, buttermilk biscuit, or tortillas. These are one of the best chilaquiles you'll ever have. Since they use their award-winning salsa, the tortilla strips absorb the flavors of the tomatoes, onions, and spices. It has a slightly spicy kick but is not overwhelming. The sour cream adds a creamy cooling quality to finish it off. Rating: 4.5/5

One Biscuit and Country Gravy ($3) is really a meal in itself. The homemade buttermilk biscuits are gigante! They are light and fluffy and you can tell that they are freshly baked that morning. The gravy has a great peppery sausage flavor with a creamy texture. Rating: 4.9/5

Avocado Eggs Benedict ($12) is two poached eggs on grilled English muffins with grilled tomatoes, two slices of ham, and topped with creamy hollandaise sauce and sliced avocado. The creamy hollandaise works excellently with the buttery avocado. The thick-sliced ham adds a meaty texture and saltiness to the dish. The perfectly poached eggs have flowing liquid gold yolks and the tomato adds a hint of sweetness. Rating: 4.5/5

Chile Verde Omelet (look for this as a special) is beautifully made with tender pork chunks in a slight spicy chile verde sauce. The cheese is gooey inside and also melted on top. It is a wonderful fusion of an American style omelet with Mexican flavors. Rating: 4.4/5</review>

< Review>
Despite my complaint, I gotta admit that their food tastes great. I'd say it's one of the better Greek restaurants. But frankly, it's disgusting when my friends and I find a hair strand every two months.

First time it happened was in January and we let it go because we understood that everyone's prone to mistake. Second time it happened was in March and we notified the owner and manager; I noticed that some employees weren't wearing head wraps so I told them about it. They said they'll be careful. It happened for the third time today.

This has been going on every third or fourth order we placed for the past seven months, which is a clear sign that the owner and managers fail to acknowledge this problem and don't care about fixing it.

And this is for some doubters out there: No, we did not finish more than half of the dish and returned it for refund or coupon.

It's disgusting. If they can't even prevent the most basic issue like this, imagine countless other sanitation issues that are ongoing in the kitchen. This restaurant's cleanliness and sanitation is way below normal.

Don't go to this restaurant; it's disgusting and its owner and managers don't care if you swallow a strand of hair in your plate or gyro. If you still go here, enjoy looking out for a strand of hair before taking every bite.<//Review>

< Review>
I had a large bedspread that needed a big, front loading machine, so I went to Carlin's. No quarters here, it works off a stored value card. There's a dollar left on my card, to get me to come back. There's one or two guys on cell phones using Carlin's Laundromat as their office, but the adjacent Carlin's cafe is quiet. There's free wifi in both places. And yes, the bedspread came out looking good.</Review>
